<span id="freeTextContainer14034344589103214584"><br/>Darkest Mercy was pretty much everything I thought it would be. Melissa Marr tied up all the loose ends from the previous novels in the series. <br/><br/>I wasn't super thrilled to read this book because, as usual, Melissa Marr's writing style tends to throw me for a loop initially. But I quickly became enthralled in the story. I was excited to see that most of the book was full of startling revelations from all of our characters.   <span id="freeText14034344589103214584" style="display:none"><br />Darkest Mercy was pretty much everything I thought it would be. Melissa Marr tied up all the loose ends from the previous novels in the series. <br /><br />I wasn't super thrilled to read this book because, as usual, Melissa Marr's writing style tends to throw me for a loop initially. But I quickly became enthralled in the story. I was excited to see that most of the book was full of startling revelations from all of our characters. It was definitely enough to keep me turning pages. <br /><br />In the final Wicked Lovely novel, we finally have the opportunity to see how far the characters have developed. Ash, in my opinion, is the most changed. She is now a confident Summer Queen. Keenan has finally realized manipulating people will get him nowhere, fast. Seth seemed to be the same to me, if anything, a little wiser. Donia learned how to release some of her bitter frost, finding happiness. <br /><br />I really would have liked to see more of Rea, Devlin, Rabbit, and Ani. I think Devlin had one line in this book, while Rea, Rabbit, and Ani were only briefly mentioned. And I won't even begin to try and understand Leslie and The Dark Kings' relationship. @@<br /><br />All in all, it was a satisfying read. <br /><br />More reviews and more at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>

<div id="review_129713443" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129713443" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129713443?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=swoooooon">swoooooon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=paranormal-ya">paranormal-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129713443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11616900173704671337">I've delayed my review of Darkest Mercy for two days because I'm not sure what I want to write. <br/>First, that i am disappointed -this is, by far, the worst in the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/305234.Wicked_Lovely__Wicked_Lovely___1_' title='Wicked Lovely (Wicked Lovely, #1) by Melissa Marr' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wicked Lovely</a> series. And it is really a pity because, being the final installment, it kind of spoils my general impression on the series. I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/305234.Wicked_Lovely__Wicked_Lovely___1_' title='Wicked Lovely (Wicked Lovely, #1) by Melissa Marr' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wicked Lovely</a> and even <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2321296.Ink_Exchange__Wicked_Lovely___2_' title='Ink Exchange (Wicked Lovely, #2) by Melissa Marr' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ink Exchange</a>, which was my least favorite, is better than this.<br/>The plot is confusing to put it mildly, and there is really no action throughout all the book, save for th</span>
  <span id="freeText11616900173704671337" style="display:none">I've delayed my review of Darkest Mercy for two days because I'm not sure what I want to write. <br />First, that i am disappointed -this is, by far, the worst in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/305234.Wicked_Lovely__Wicked_Lovely___1_" title="Wicked Lovely (Wicked Lovely, #1) by Melissa Marr" rel="nofollow noopener">Wicked Lovely</a> series. And it is really a pity because, being the final installment, it kind of spoils my general impression on the series. I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/305234.Wicked_Lovely__Wicked_Lovely___1_" title="Wicked Lovely (Wicked Lovely, #1) by Melissa Marr" rel="nofollow noopener">Wicked Lovely</a> and even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2321296.Ink_Exchange__Wicked_Lovely___2_" title="Ink Exchange (Wicked Lovely, #2) by Melissa Marr" rel="nofollow noopener">Ink Exchange</a>, which was my least favorite, is better than this.<br />The plot is confusing to put it mildly, and there is really no action throughout all the book, save for the epic X-Men-like battle at the end. <br />Characters I loved, Ash, Keenan, Donia, Seth, Niall, in this book are just going around Huntsdale visiting each other and having pointless conversations, so much so that at times I couldn't even understand the reason in the economy of the plot of said conversations. <br /><br />Keenan and Donia - I wanted to strangle them both. Their continuous indecisiveness got on my nerves - i could understand the problems behind their being together but their constant changes of mind were really too much, especially from Keenan. I could not feel his torment for not being able to be with Donia and it seemed to me that, if Ash had let him in her bed, he would have been more than happy about it. BUT she refuses him and, after 4 books, he finally decides he needs to be with the one he really loves and dumps Ash and the Summer Court. And Donia? Who loved him for ages, got cheated, deceived, exploited, what does she do when he goes begging to her, the dog? FORGIVES HIM! No questions asked. Not even one doubt. This is SO not how a woman should be treated or how she should react in such a situation. Bad, bad example. <br />Ash and Seth have somehow slightly better roles but again, Seth, big disappointment. At the end, when there is finally some action, he sits out. Like really, he is sitting in a cage reading his newspaper and smoking a ciggie. The balance to Darkness, my ass. <br />The only character i did probably like in this book is Far Dorcha, the Death-fey, even though i was laughing when I pictured ethereal sister Ankou hauling corpses on a van, going about the battlefield, whistling to herself.<br /><br />So, Marr gave us a - rather bloody - happy ending for everybody - except poor Gabriel who went into a pointless battle, got killed and forgotten in 10 pages. Reading this book gave me closure, of which I am happy but I am VERY disappointed by the execution and the plot. I'd never have thought I'd be tempted ti skip pages on a Melissa Marr's book. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11616900173704671337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_130432871" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130432871" />
    <a title="Pamela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3645538-pamela"><img alt="Pamela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535386427p2/3645538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130432871?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/3645538-pamela">Pamela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3645538-pamela?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130432871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10506247645402268881">I was so shocked when I found out that the Wicked Lovely series is the first series I’ve finished in three months. This was supposed to make me sad and all that, but all it made me feel was relieved.<br/><br/>Anyway, I read somewhere that something was going to happen at the beginning of this book so I was shocked when I found out that this specific event happened past page 100. That was the beginning? What do you call the previous hundred pages, the prologue? And speaking of the real beginning, I was ete</span>
  <span id="freeText10506247645402268881" style="display:none">I was so shocked when I found out that the Wicked Lovely series is the first series I’ve finished in three months. This was supposed to make me sad and all that, but all it made me feel was relieved.<br /><br />Anyway, I read somewhere that something was going to happen at the beginning of this book so I was shocked when I found out that this specific event happened past page 100. That was the beginning? What do you call the previous hundred pages, the prologue? And speaking of the real beginning, I was eternally annoyed at Donia and Keenan’s chapters, and of Aislinn’s too. There was just too many things that were irrelevant to me. I also hated one chapter of Seth’s because it was a repeat of the final chapter of Radiant Shadows. I really don’t need to read a chapter twice to understand it. This chapter was a complete waste of paper.<br /><br />Speaking of wasting of paper, I believe that the whole series could be fit into one book. Why? Because there were so many things that needn’t be said but was there anyway.<br /><br />There were also a lot of mistakes in the book but I don’t think I want to discuss it anymore since I’m free of the series and can now move on with my life.<br /><br />The fighting scenes weren’t convincing. It says that there were a lot of faeries in the room but some of the others are just standing around and not being attacked? That’s impossible.<br /><br />And I now officially hate switching perspectives because instead of getting each character’s different insights, I get NONE.<br /><br />Nevertheless, I must admit that I would miss this series. It’s one that I’ve read and have journeyed with so it’s a bit sad that it’s all done now. I am grateful that I’m done with the series though. LOL, do I even make any sense?<br /><br />I don’t think the ending was all that great. Everyone was just in everyone’s pants. Except Chela. Poor, poor Chela.<br /><br />Overall, I guess you should read this if you want to finish the series (as I did) but if you don’t, you can skip this one.<br /><br />Oh, maybe I should add my midnight reading insight here. I typed it out on my phone so I’ll just copy it. I won’t edit it anymore:<br /><br />I got it! The reason why Donia and Keenan don’t seem to love each other is because Keenan never showed any sign that he cared for her. It’s like the author only thought of showing that now. Enter Donia: she’s like a girl who can’t figure out that she can never be with him. Ever. Now she acts all strong and distant like a stupid girl who wants vengeance but doesn’t do it either because of two things: she doesn’t know the word or she hasn’t really lived for 900 years. Melissa Marr has a small, small grasp on immortality that it’s probably nonexistent because she’s making her faery characters act like humans.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10506247645402268881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_199787968" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/199787968" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/163750-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1189653481p2/163750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/199787968?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/163750-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=fairytale-myth-legend">fairytale-myth-legend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer199787968&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199787968" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1213783586365134812">While Seth was important in several ways, continuing to be my favourite character in the series as he made it possible for Bananach to be defeated, I didn't like how he was pushed off onto the sidelines for most of the action, even though he'd been training to fight in the inevitable battle. <br/>I wanted something else for poor Niall, my second-favourite character in the series, but he seemed more broken than ever. <br/>Sorcha was relegated to a small part as worried but inactive mother and not seen agai</span>
  <span id="freeText1213783586365134812" style="display:none">While Seth was important in several ways, continuing to be my favourite character in the series as he made it possible for Bananach to be defeated, I didn't like how he was pushed off onto the sidelines for most of the action, even though he'd been training to fight in the inevitable battle. <br />I wanted something else for poor Niall, my second-favourite character in the series, but he seemed more broken than ever. <br />Sorcha was relegated to a small part as worried but inactive mother and not seen again. <br />Given that book 4 was devoted to them, I'd expected Devlin and Ani to figure significantly in the final book of the series; but they didn't. <br />The book did surprise me several times with plot twists. Some things I never saw coming. <br />I very much liked that the two main couples ended up with the right people and got happy endings. <br />Keenan did some things I never expected him to do and turned out to be not so bad, after all. It was nice that Keenan finally put Donia first. <br />I was glad that Aislinn didn't do anything stupid with Keenan. I liked how it took time for Seth and Aislinn to work out their troubles, but they were still true to each other even during the difficult times.<br />Aislinn and Donia became stronger characters, and it was good that they both had to deal with major concerns that put their love lives on the back burner for a while. The way Aislinn did most of the work in defeating the evil Bananach (Niall did help finish her off) and rescued Seth was very impressive. Donia put her subjects first and was willing to broker deals with the other courts for the good of all and did her share of fierce fighting, too (her ice swords are nifty).<br /> <i>Wicked Lovely</i> has a rather positive message for girls, in terms of choices and power. Love is very important in the <i>Wicked Lovely</i> world, but there are other significant things, too. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1213783586365134812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1628485916" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1628485916" />
    <a title="☆Stephanie☆" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20199767-stephanie"><img alt="☆Stephanie☆" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521760196p2/20199767.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1628485916?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☆Stephanie☆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☆Stephanie☆" href="/user/show/20199767-stephanie">☆Stephanie☆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20199767-stephanie?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20199767-stephanie?shelf=ya-paranormal">ya-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20199767-stephanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20199767-stephanie?shelf=ya-fairies">ya-fairies</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1628485916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16506480110923491917">I finished it...and my heart is broken.<br/>I knew I was going to have to finish it eventually...and now the <i>Wicked Lovely</i> series is done. Finito. No more. I sigh in sadness.<br/>I know what you'll say..."But, Stephanie, there's still <i>Desert Tales</i> and <i>Fairy Tales and Nighmares</i>, plus <i>Love Struck</i> which is a novella set with water fae. Yes, there are still a couple offshoots of the main storyline, but it's not the same. Oh, yes, I'll read them, but the core series is done. Ash and Seth and Keenan and Donia a</span>
  <span id="freeText16506480110923491917" style="display:none">I finished it...and my heart is broken.<br />I knew I was going to have to finish it eventually...and now the <i>Wicked Lovely</i> series is done. Finito. No more. I sigh in sadness.<br />I know what you'll say..."But, Stephanie, there's still <i>Desert Tales</i> and <i>Fairy Tales and Nighmares</i>, plus <i>Love Struck</i> which is a novella set with water fae. Yes, there are still a couple offshoots of the main storyline, but it's not the same. Oh, yes, I'll read them, but the core series is done. Ash and Seth and Keenan and Donia and Irial and Niall....their stories are over. <br />This is why I waited so long to finish <i>Darkest Mercy</i>. Yes, I was dying to know what was going to happen, but I didn't want the adventure to be over.<br />I died a little on the inside. <br />I do hope Marr goes back to the world of fae....I do plan to read <i>Made for You</i> to see what else Marr has written...but I'd much rather see s sequel to <i>Carnival of Souls</i>...and I doubt that's going to happen with the amount of time that has passed since that book was written. <br />I don't want to write any spoilers for this book: if you've gotten this far in the series, anything I'll say will ruin all the twists and turns. Did not end how I was expecting it to, but it was a lovely ending nonetheless. Essentially, Bananach is thirsty for War, and Far Dorcha (the death fae) has appeared in the town, which is an ominous omen to all fairies that sh**'s going down. Bad stuff is going to happen...and with the veil to Fairie closed, all the fae on the mortal side of the veil are alone to face the problems themselves. And what of Ash and Seth? Will Keenan make Ash his Summer Queen in body and soul? Is Donia going to be left with a broken heart? Can Bananach really be defeated, or would it mean the end of all of the fairies? Gotta answer those questions yourself, my friends. It's worth the wait.<br />★★★★★. For the whole series, ★★★★★. Marr is a natural born storyteller, and we are fortunate to read what she writes. Beautiful and sad, magical and cruel, Marr's world of fae creatures are like nothing you've ever experienced before. Marr makes the hard choices and puts the reader on an emotional rollercoaster, but you leave it all with a smile on your face and the characters in your heart. If you can be touched, truly touched, by fictional characters, Marr makes it happen. I'll probably revisit this series one day and read it all again.<br />This is a series I would love to own and reread...and I would always be open to more from Marr and her world of fairies.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16506480110923491917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3759728-may?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3759728-may?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer2085106209248142704">I won this book for free in a first-reads giveaway. <br/><br/>I was so absolutely thrilled when this arrived in the mail! I swear, I danced around the house for half an hour. It took me forever to read, mostly because life was busy, but it was fantastic. And amazing. <br/><br/>Every book in the series is a little bittersweet. There are things lost, but things won. In Darkest Mercy, the things won over-balance the things lost, I think. It was stunning, and while I'm sad it's over, at the same time I'm thrilled! <br/><br/>~~~W</span>
  <span id="freeText2085106209248142704" style="display:none">I won this book for free in a first-reads giveaway. <br /><br />I was so absolutely thrilled when this arrived in the mail! I swear, I danced around the house for half an hour. It took me forever to read, mostly because life was busy, but it was fantastic. And amazing. <br /><br />Every book in the series is a little bittersweet. There are things lost, but things won. In Darkest Mercy, the things won over-balance the things lost, I think. It was stunning, and while I'm sad it's over, at the same time I'm thrilled! <br /><br />~~~WARNING, SPOILERS AHEAD!~~~<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />Right, you've been warned. In this book,Leslie returns when Niall is unbalanced and nearly insane, to try and fix him. As it's been a little while since I read Ink Exchange, I don't remember Leslie's character too well, but she seemed a bit over-aggressive. But then, that may be because she's still part Dark Court. <br /><br />Finally, Ash has to make a choice between Seth and Keenen. She ends up choosing Seth. I was disappointed at first, since the love triangle was so interesting, but it all ends up working out. Keenen gives her his powers as a monarch and can finally be with Donia, and at the end, Seth can finally fully be with Ash. A happy ending for them all~<br /><br />There was one little thing that bugged me, though it didn't have anything to do with the storyline. In a few places quotation marks were forgotten, periods forgotten, just a few little grammar errors like that. Other than that, the book was just amazing and I want to read it all over again! </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Any one who loves the FEY! Wicked Lovely followers, Melissa Marr lovers, YA-PNR fans</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128435404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2346549940777736313">I have followed the Wicked Lovely series since its inception and I have loved every single word. I cried at the last page because I knew that I would no longer hear from my deliciously exciting friends in their deliciously exciting world that Melissa has created so wondrously and so wickedly :o]<br/><br/>Darkest Mercy held some surprises but not as many as I would have suspected and I thank Melissa for that; there is the loss of one character that I absolutely adored, starting in The Ink Exchange & Radian</span>
  <span id="freeText2346549940777736313" style="display:none">I have followed the Wicked Lovely series since its inception and I have loved every single word. I cried at the last page because I knew that I would no longer hear from my deliciously exciting friends in their deliciously exciting world that Melissa has created so wondrously and so wickedly :o]<br /><br />Darkest Mercy held some surprises but not as many as I would have suspected and I thank Melissa for that; there is the loss of one character that I absolutely adored, starting in The Ink Exchange &amp; Radiant Shadows. It seemed so minimized in Darkest Mercy and that kind of bothered me but other then that Darkest Mercy was the perfect ending to a perfect series.<br /><br />Melissa created a beautiful story to end her series and in fact, as gruesome as this may sound, Darkest Mercy was almost a memoriam to our beloved characters and the beautiful world she created. I do believe her characters will go on in our hearts for they've become real to so many of us that saying good bye is extremely difficult (Hence the tears at the last page) that the grieving process is necessary for some, if not all, of her Wicked Lovely fans. As much as I looked forward to reading Darkest Mercy, I also dreaded it. I dreaded it for the mere fact that Darkest Mercy was the LAST book, not like some who say it’s the last book and then dangle another book in front of our faces at the last minute.<br /> <br />So, with much sadness in my heart I will say ‘see ya later’ to the Courts for now but I will never good-bye because I know that they will always be a book shelf away and definitely live on forever in my heart.<br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=own-arc">own-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=signed-arcs">signed-arcs</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107155780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12623463197456957463">Darkest Mercy was more than a just satisfying ending to an unforgettable series.... it was brilliant. Epic even. I shall miss it.<br/><br/>Let me just get this out of the way right now. That whole thing with Keenan... how painfully obvious was that! I mean seriously.... did you give yourself the duh slap with that one, or what!?!? And for those of you that haven't read it yet, that won't probably mean anything, sorry about that.<br/><br/>I love this story and I love the characters. I'm going to miss them so much! U</span>
  <span id="freeText12623463197456957463" style="display:none">Darkest Mercy was more than a just satisfying ending to an unforgettable series.... it was brilliant. Epic even. I shall miss it.<br /><br />Let me just get this out of the way right now. That whole thing with Keenan... how painfully obvious was that! I mean seriously.... did you give yourself the duh slap with that one, or what!?!? And for those of you that haven't read it yet, that won't probably mean anything, sorry about that.<br /><br />I love this story and I love the characters. I'm going to miss them so much! Usually I enjoy a certain character because I can relate to them, honestly there wasn't any character that I felt I could relate to in these novels. I mean they're bad-ass... tattoos, piercings... dangerous fae.... but they are FASCINATING! I couldn't help but come to love each and every one of them.<br /><br />Marr did an excellent job creating threads in each novel and finally weaving them together to make this stunning ending a masterpiece..... loved it. There are so many story lines one might find it easy to become confused but somehow Marr makes it work, and makes it work wonderfully well. Did I mention I loved it? I was actually hesitant to start this one because I didn't want it to end, but once I started I couldn't put it down. I didn't put it down until the last page was turned.<br /><br />If you haven't read this series I recommend that you do! Can't wait to see what Marr has for us next!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12623463197456957463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Rxlm9b5DSkvDP/e5HixE77lDoG3DYu0oC7GJ/pU51h7Mk7uFgNu0njVjo8hH/xVhAK3ADXmAf6HaX6/oS9SQSA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hracRI73P+iaGIVAdWCkbrON+b8c1DT6iJd4pT1kZ/8NPEE0sG/BPWxE0TEss/XgCmOZ36Y2pnNZeV6z44khqQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4295702692875071646"><br/>Melissa Marr is a former university literature instructor who writes fiction for adults, teens, and children. She is best known for the Wicked Lovely series for teens, the Graveminder for adults, and her debut picturebook Bunny Roo, I Love You. <br/><br/>Her books have been translated into twenty-eight languages and been bestsellers internationally as well as domestically (NY Times, Los Angeles Times, USA T</span>
  <span id="freeText4295702692875071646" style="display:none"><br />Melissa Marr is a former university literature instructor who writes fiction for adults, teens, and children. She is best known for the Wicked Lovely series for teens, the Graveminder for adults, and her debut picturebook Bunny Roo, I Love You. <br /><br />Her books have been translated into twenty-eight languages and been bestsellers internationally as well as domestically (NY Times, Los Angeles Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal).Accolades include starred reviews on numerous books, YALSA Popular Paperbacks, IRA Notable Book Pick, Book Sense Pick (YA and adult), Good Morning America Summer Pick for Teens, Scottish Book Trust, Red Maple finalist (in both Ontario and Manitoba), and Goodreads Good Choice Award (Horror), RWA RITA award (YA). <br /><br />She also write romance for adults as Ronnie Douglas.<br /><br />She co-authored (with Kelley Armstrong) a MG trilogy as M.A. Marr. <br /><br />In addition to novels, Melissa has co-edited several anthologies, as well as published short fiction, manga, and prose non-fiction. <br /><br />She currently lives with her family in Arizona.</span>
